  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0c319036-a455-4ae3-abc0-91a6fec07f0c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1904910877728340193">Based on true events, but unlike anything you've ever read before, #1 New York Times bestselling author Nelson DeMille has created what may be his finest work to date.<br/><br/>It is dusk on July 17, 1996.   <span id="freeText1904910877728340193" style="display:none">Based on true events, but unlike anything you've ever read before, #1 New York Times bestselling author Nelson DeMille has created what may be his finest work to date.<br /><br />It is dusk on July 17, 1996. A man and a woman who are married--but not to each other--make love on a Long Island beach as a video camera records their pleasure...and something more. Out over the ocean, TWA Flight 800 suddenly explodes with 230 victims on board, the terrible blast illuminating the sky. The government's verdict is mechanical failure. But the videotape may tell another story--if it can be found.<br /><br />Now on the fifth anniversary of the crash, two members of the Federal Anti-Terrorist Task Force set out to reopen the case; John Corey, an ex-NYPD detective, and his wife, Kate Mayfield, a career FBI agent. Together, they hunt for the crucial video...and race towed an elusive truth even more horrifying than the crash itself.<br />--back cover</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362748300" />
    <a title="Tim Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10746396-tim-williams"><img alt="Tim Williams" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362748300?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim Williams" href="/user/show/10746396-tim-williams">Tim Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362748300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14376839664482519567">This book was 692 pages. For 690 pages it was one of the best books I've ever read and then DeMille completely ruined it with one of the most piece-of-crap, cop-out endings I've ever seen coming a mile away. He even admits that he had no idea how to finish this book and his son came up with the idea for the ending. I guess that's the problem with writing a story based on a real-life event. You can't really change history or present "facts" that didn't actually happen, so he completely wrote hims</span>
  <span id="freeText14376839664482519567" style="display:none">This book was 692 pages. For 690 pages it was one of the best books I've ever read and then DeMille completely ruined it with one of the most piece-of-crap, cop-out endings I've ever seen coming a mile away. He even admits that he had no idea how to finish this book and his son came up with the idea for the ending. I guess that's the problem with writing a story based on a real-life event. You can't really change history or present "facts" that didn't actually happen, so he completely wrote himself into a corner and had to find a way out.<br /><br />I was 3/4 of the way through this book and had it not been so late at night, I would've immediately gone out to the bookstore and bought everything he had ever written. I'm not picking up another one of his books now. <br /><br />Seriously, the ending of this book is just brutal and it completely ruins how outstanding the rest of the book was. I'm getting disappointed all over again as I write this review. I was actively angry when I finished the book because of what a dumpster-fire on an ending it has.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14376839664482519567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1923835135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923835135" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923835135?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of thrillers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      Sharon, Alfred, Don
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923835135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11575437776145669946">Generally, I’m not a fan of political thrillers. You say to me, “Carol, here’s a political thriller I just know you will love…” and I will not be rushing to the library or my favorite dealer to get a copy. Frankly, I find most of them silly and poorly written. Government conspiracies? Puh-leaze.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489470817i/22217164.jpg' width='260' height='260' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Not so believable.</i><br/><br/>At any rate, this one popped up in discussion and due to enthusiasm from Sharon and recommendations from Alfred (and others, I think–I lost the thread), Sharon and I decided to give it t</span>
  <span id="freeText11575437776145669946" style="display:none">Generally, I’m not a fan of political thrillers. You say to me, “Carol, here’s a political thriller I just know you will love…” and I will not be rushing to the library or my favorite dealer to get a copy. Frankly, I find most of them silly and poorly written. Government conspiracies? Puh-leaze.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489470817i/22217164.jpg" width="260" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Not so believable.</i><br><br>At any rate, this one popped up in discussion and due to enthusiasm from Sharon and recommendations from Alfred (and others, I think–I lost the thread), Sharon and I decided to give it the buddy read treatment.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489470817ra/22217165.gif" width="280" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I'm not a very good reading best friend. because I’m completely one of those people that talks while reading. Or updates. Or tends to drop spoilers. Or really, really wants to share quotes. </i><br><br>John Corey is a rather typical, maverick cop, an ex- NYPD detective who now works with the FBI on part of a dedicated terrorist task force with his wife, a FBI agent herself. Like all great detectives, she has a case that haunts her with its lack of resolution. She persuades John to go with her to the memorial for TWA Flight 800, a Paris-bound airline that broke apart due to ‘mechanical failure,’ killing everyone on board. At the memorial, a CIA agent that John has a highly antagonistic relationship with warns John to let the case be.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489470817ra/22217166.gif" width="310" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Like waving a red flag</i><br><br>John finds himself playing devil’s advocate as Kate gradually takes him through the details of the case, but when they get to an unshakable eye-witness who swears he saw what seemed to be a missile, even John feels niggling doubts. He knows he has to work fast to make progress before he is shut down by his superiors. DeMille is clever with pacing in this book. It begins with a lurid sex scene hinting at potential video tape, and then moves into detailed background building of the investigation of a crashed plane. It could have easily been boring, but I was quickly engrossed in the details, and I enjoyed the complex motivation of justice, stubbornness and independence that keeps John on the case.<br><b><br>“But it wasn’t about Kate or me, or anyone else, in or out of the government. It was about them. 230 of them. And their families and loved ones, the people who had placed roses on the seats of the aircraft, and who had lit the candles and waded into the ocean, and thrown the flowers into the sea. And the people who haven’t been at the service, who sat at home tonight and cried.”<br></b><br>John uses old contacts in the NYPD to do some investigating, and doggedly tracks the pieces leading to the potential videotape. There was a very police procedural aspect to it; it felt real, somewhat slowly methodical, and somewhat maddening as John runs into leads seemingly dead-ended by… someone. Meanwhile, superiors at the Task Force are bringing pressure to bear and threatening both him and Kate. It morphs into a thriller, leading me to turn pages faster and faster by the end.<br><br>I enjoyed the characterization. I found John to be rather typical of the maverick detective school; the one who is willing to flaunt authority, but because of his amazing skill remains useful and not completely ostracized. He is, of course, very attractive to the ladies, but avoids further entanglements due to his commitment to Kate. Kate was an interesting foil whose lingering compassion for the loved ones sets off an investigation she is ambivalent about. Although never really fleshed out well, we get a sense that John both loves and respects her, despite occasionally antagonistic behaviors. In fact, they felt like a real couple. I immediately wanted to read more books with him and thought of starting with the first, Plum Island, but basically heard he was exponentially more of a chauvinist (or the writing was) in that one, so it’s a pass until I need a rant-read.<br><br>Plotting was solid, with a couple of quirks that will linger.<br><br>MILD SPOILER: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ at one point, Kate and John are sent on separate missions overseas for the Task Force. It seemed an odd authorial transition, but was most likely an attempt to bring in more question of international terrorist cell involvement. The section was generally underwritten, and didn’t seem to add much to the story, although John did lose the beer weight he was carrying. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>VERY MILD SPOILER: I ended up reading faster and faster, but it was the end that was pretty much a solid punch in the face.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489470817ra/22217167.gif" width="320" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I looked a lot like Crowley at the end, without the cuts. </i><br><br>Let’s just say that thanks to Tana French, I know how to take a punch. It was appropriate, but I can appreciate it pissed some readers off.<br><br>Overall, a super-engrossing read. Perfect for a sick day with a head cold, where I was completely taken out of my own physical tissue-wasting experience and not thrown back into reality by hack writing. I’ll check out more DeMille.<br><br>Thanks, Sharon!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489470963i/22217177._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11575437776145669946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_974344582" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/974344582" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/974344582?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer974344582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10707604905205161340">Oh my god. No amount of planning could prepare me to pen a deserving review for Night Fall. I will never ever read such a large book in so short a time. It was unbelievable. This is why I read books. After this, if I have to ditch 10 books in a row, it will be worth it. When I was reading Night Fall, I thought no way does this book get 4/5 stars. But it occurred that all events converged on the remaining chapters. That is the only way an okay setup book jumps from okay to amazing. The most recen</span>
  <span id="freeText10707604905205161340" style="display:none">Oh my god. No amount of planning could prepare me to pen a deserving review for Night Fall. I will never ever read such a large book in so short a time. It was unbelievable. This is why I read books. After this, if I have to ditch 10 books in a row, it will be worth it. When I was reading Night Fall, I thought no way does this book get 4/5 stars. But it occurred that all events converged on the remaining chapters. That is the only way an okay setup book jumps from okay to amazing. The most recent film that I've seen that had that structure was Miyazaki's The Wind Rises. The end made the preceding story spine tingling. <br /><br /> I want to convince you that Night Fall is an amazing book. You should read it. Reading, for the moment for me, is so much better than movies or music. It's the remaining medium in which I have faith and which delivers more often than not. Night Fall comprises of 672 pages. I went through them like that. For a story of its type there were few people to keep track of. John Corey always surprises me. He keeps needing to remind me that he does detect and solves mysteries, which is usually not the priority in the twist obsessed world of the thriller.<br /><br /> The genius thing about this book is when the hero and his wife are exiled from the USA. We don't see their extradition. Bang, immediately in the next chapter Corey returns home, and takes up the forbidden, conspiracy laced case and follows its trail from the airport. I will not trade that moment for any other memory of any book that I've read. Take a bow Nelson Demille, for this book is surely your masterpiece. I feel strongly about the Jill Winslow character. She was a real tragic figure, and I was against her in the beginning. What a turnaround. This is what good art does. It plays with our emotions without making us aware of the manipulation. I will re read this book soon. I have to. I'm still not sure how this embarking became a stroll in the park.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10707604905205161340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1923361912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923361912" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/671638-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471996534p2/671638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923361912?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/671638-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923361912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10711888603160766345">This book and I may have gotten off on the wrong foot. I wanted to revisit Nelson DeMille--I read <i>Plum Island</i> years ago and remembered really enjoying it, especially protagonist John Corey's smartass sense of humor. I recall very little about the book, other than a row between Corey and a villain which ends up with Corey disemboweling him, and proceeding to lay the contents on his open stomach with a flourish (<i>"'Your guts,' I declared."</i>). That's a line that stays with you when you're young.<br/><br/>Upon </span>
  <span id="freeText10711888603160766345" style="display:none">This book and I may have gotten off on the wrong foot. I wanted to revisit Nelson DeMille--I read <i>Plum Island</i> years ago and remembered really enjoying it, especially protagonist John Corey's smartass sense of humor. I recall very little about the book, other than a row between Corey and a villain which ends up with Corey disemboweling him, and proceeding to lay the contents on his open stomach with a flourish (<i>"'Your guts,' I declared."</i>). That's a line that stays with you when you're young.<br /><br />Upon recommendation (thanks, Don!), I picked up <i>Night Fall</i>, not giving the synopsis a glance. This may have been an issue, as the whole book deals with speculation and conspiracy theories surrounding TWA Flight 800, which exploded off the coast of Long Island in 1996. I had just graduated from high school and remember hearing the news quite vividly. I remember all of the initial eye-witness accounts reporting what seemed to be a missile heading towards the plane before its explosion, and then how all of those reports seemed to just die down. Mechanical trouble, the final report stated.<br /><br />DeMille gives a great forward about why he felt compelled to write about the explosion--exploring multiple theories, including the official conclusion--framing events and eye-witness accounts within a fictional detective yarn. Part of me was up for the journey. Who doesn't like a good conspiracy theory?<br /><br />The other part of me was conflicted about the subject matter. What I liked most about DeMille's main guy last time around was his sarcasm, and I just didn't know if I could stomach sarcasm or jokes about something that felt like it happened yesterday. I've suffered from a fear of flying my whole life, so when I hear about a plane crash, hijacking, etc., I go to a bad place.... and stay there. For an uncomfortable amount of time. It's a tragic event, and while I think DeMille's intentions were good, this obviously impacted any pleasure I was hoping to glean from a light, fun read. I mean, I was BUDDY READING this book! (More on that later.)<br /><br />Anyway, I read somewhere once in "the rules of crime-solving" that a detective can't solve a case until he turns in his gun and his badge; that any grocery bag has to have a baguette peaking out from the top; that a man can take a gunshot wound like a champ but will flinch in distress if a woman is cleaning out his paper cut--many of these cliches hold true in this novel, but DeMille is clever enough to make them part of the fun. And as the story moves farther from the details of the crash, and deeper into the intricacies of Corey's detective work and one-liners, I felt my enjoyment cautiously growing. Nelson knows how to get you to turn those pages, and as Corey's wife Kate must do on multiple occasions, you just want to roll your eyes when Corey's being the colossal dick he fully acknowledges he's being. ... And then give him a big old bear hug and say fondly, "oh, John."<br /><br />...Until all enjoyment abruptly stopped. When I registered where the final pages were headed (and I had my suspicions early on), I couldn't help feeling tricked and disappointed. Harsh? Maybe. But in the interest of being spoiler-free, let's just say my initial intuition that the subject matter was too much for me was accurate. And I certainly didn't get the resolution that is so satisfying in detective novels.<br /><br />Would I read another DeMille? I would; he knows how to write page turners, and make me chuckle. This just happened to be the wrong pick for yours truly. Rating: 4 for readability, 2 for subject matter, 2 when I compare it to the other DeMille I've read, <i>Plum Island</i>. 5 for book-club worthiness. I settled on a 3.<br /><br />This marks the second book of the year that I have "buddy read." The first being <i>The End of the Affair</i> with Joe Valdez (spoiler: He hated it! I loved it!); this one with whip-smart Carol. I love all "you people" on Goodreads, but Carol is one of my faves. I always look forward to her smart, opinionated reviews: she has a critical, discerning eye, which she applies to any genre she reads: fantasy, sci-fi, mystery. She loves strong women, kickass authors like Octavia Butler, and when I picture her writing her reviews, I picture her thoughtfully staring into space like her awesome avatar. I also discovered quite recently that she is a speed reader :) Check out her review of <i>Dune</i>; you won't regret it.<br /><br />I'm very curious to see where Carol lands with <i>Night Fall</i>, but regardless of her final rating, I'm sure I'll enjoy the review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10711888603160766345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1226950105" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1226950105" />
    <a title="Freda Malone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone"><img alt="Freda Malone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418039583p2/6938113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1226950105?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freda Malone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freda Malone" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone">Freda Malone</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1226950105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2277280269770684741">Wow. I'm shattered, shocked and awed by this novel. Pay special close attention to the time frame in the book. TWA Flight 800 tragedy 1996, the 5 year anniversary 2001. I was so engrossed in this fast paced, action packed, novel that I absolutely did not see the end coming. “Holy Shit” I said to myself and “No Way”. I had to go back and look. When you read this you'll be in for the ride of your life and the tension will grow and grow, and you will become shattered at the end. I hate cliffhangers</span>
  <span id="freeText2277280269770684741" style="display:none">Wow. I'm shattered, shocked and awed by this novel. Pay special close attention to the time frame in the book. TWA Flight 800 tragedy 1996, the 5 year anniversary 2001. I was so engrossed in this fast paced, action packed, novel that I absolutely did not see the end coming. “Holy Shit” I said to myself and “No Way”. I had to go back and look. When you read this you'll be in for the ride of your life and the tension will grow and grow, and you will become shattered at the end. I hate cliffhangers but I'll make an exception this ONE time and only because this thriller was written by a mastermind of a writer. Nelson DeMille is sneaky, clever, and just downright astonishingly intelligent when it comes to creative writing. Just WOW. <br /><br />John Corey is still his obnoxiously sarcastic self and one of the most fun alpha males in the fictional world and he kicks butt. For truth, for justice and with much patriotism as well as ‘doing the right thing’. However, in the real world, he would not get any second, third or fourth chances and so some of DeMille’s choices in his writing can be a ‘roll eyes’, ‘yeah, right’, type of read but quite entertaining!<br /><br />READ THIS BOOK! It will shatter you too!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2277280269770684741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15673554922761860317">Demille's books seem to be reliably good (at least this series has been so far). I'm getting these from the public library (hey, I'm already looking at having to reduce the size of my own library...a lot. i can't buy every book I read). That means i usually have to put these on hold and wait to get them.<br/><br/>As I did this one.<br/><br/>This volume of the lives of our heros begins a little more slowly or maybe I should use the word "obliquely" than the first two.   <span id="freeText15673554922761860317" style="display:none">Demille's books seem to be reliably good (at least this series has been so far). I'm getting these from the public library (hey, I'm already looking at having to reduce the size of my own library...a lot. i can't buy every book I read). That means i usually have to put these on hold and wait to get them.<br /><br />As I did this one.<br /><br />This volume of the lives of our heros begins a little more slowly or maybe I should use the word "obliquely" than the first two. Hang in there it will grab you.<br /><br />Kate (Mayfield) has ghosts haunting her and as the book opens a particularly tricky and dangerous one. <br /><br />And she gets John (Corey) involved.<br /><br />Things go down a somewhat predictable road after that but there are enough twists and turns leading to the strange conclusion that it's all worth it.<br /><br />And be ready to want the next novel. Recommended. Enjoy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16851024404018242266">Once again Mark Twain’s formula for an American crime writer of killing everybody off at the end is followed. This time September 11th does it, wiping out witnesses and conspirators alike. Too bad!!<br/>	For almost 500 pages we surely want to know who targeted this flight and why was there a cover-up?<br/>	There is much humour and suspense through-out but the essentials are unanswered.<br/> <br/></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chipper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chipper" href="/user/show/2806902-chipper">Chipper</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73487695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6548142870793505307">DeMille's wit is in full effect in the suspenseful thriller! Made me laugh over and over and over again. The characters are likeable and believable, the story has the right level of sophistication and many of the theories in the book are based on verifiable facts and eyewitness statements regarding TWA Flight 800. Some readers have been and will continue to be displeased by the last couple pages. I, on the other hand, felt it was a perfect conclusion to a fastastic and wildly entertaining story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110135362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110135362" />
    <a title="Jerry B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3901425-jerry-b"><img alt="Jerry B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412552940p2/3901425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110135362?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry B" href="/user/show/3901425-jerry-b">Jerry B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110135362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12790681300463481865">Suspenseful tale built on TWA-800 crash - but sloppy ending!<br/><br/>We are loyal followers of DeMille's entire bibliography, so looked forward to "Night Fall", especially once we got the drift it was based on fact and embellished with fiction (ala the Da Vinci Code). The author concocts two eyewitnesses to the crash of TWA flight 800 in 1996, who not only claimed to have seen a "missile" streak skyward toward the plane, but may have videotaped it as well, as part of a secret, sex-filled beachside rendez</span>
  <span id="freeText12790681300463481865" style="display:none">Suspenseful tale built on TWA-800 crash - but sloppy ending!<br /><br />We are loyal followers of DeMille's entire bibliography, so looked forward to "Night Fall", especially once we got the drift it was based on fact and embellished with fiction (ala the Da Vinci Code). The author concocts two eyewitnesses to the crash of TWA flight 800 in 1996, who not only claimed to have seen a "missile" streak skyward toward the plane, but may have videotaped it as well, as part of a secret, sex-filled beachside rendezvous! Enter John Corey (from Demille's "Plum Island" and "Gold Coast"), now part of an FBI anti-terrorist task force, and now married to Kate Mayfield, another FBI-type who personally interviewed many of the some 200 people who also claimed to have seen a missile-like object heading toward the plane. Corey attends a 5-year memorial service re the tragedy and starts looking into matters never very well resolved by the official explanation of mechanical failure that brought down the airliner. He doesn't know about the sexy couple at first like we do, but sensing a conspiracy or cover-up, pursues them all book-long in a suspenseful prelude to a showdown with federal officials. The book ends in a predictable yet unexpected fashion -- and the loose ends left flapping bothered us a bit just as it did many other readers. <br /><br />DeMille has written a clever book that makes the pages fly. As the timeline of the book proceeded throughout 2001 toward that now fateful day of infamy, we wondered how he would handle the outcome of his main story. To us, the abrupt dissatisfaction of the ending detracted from an otherwise well crafted yarn - one that looks to be backed up with substantial research. Give us a better ending, and a fifth star would be no problem! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12790681300463481865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224854866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224854866" />
    <a title="Trix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4450624-trix"><img alt="Trix" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417957933p2/4450624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224854866?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trix" href="/user/show/4450624-trix">Trix</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780751531800" href="/book/show/945081.Night_Fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=hard-copy">hard-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=cops">cops</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=terrorism">terrorism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4450624-trix?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224854866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15927426953227097846">I liked this book much more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33808.The_Lion_s_Game__John_Corey___2_' title='The Lion's Game (John Corey, #2) by Nelson DeMille' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion's Game</a>. I suspect it has a lot to do with the fact that this story had more of the hands-on approach than the rest. Whereas the 'mystery' in the previous Corey book was solved in the last pages of the book, "Night Fall" was shrouded in mystery to the end and only slowly revealed its secrets.<br/><br/>John Corey seemed to be more in his element in this book. Or perhaps, all that chasing around masked some of the cynicism and bravado. Don't get me wrong, I like his </span>
  <span id="freeText15927426953227097846" style="display:none">I liked this book much more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33808.The_Lion_s_Game__John_Corey___2_" title="The Lion's Game (John Corey, #2) by Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion's Game</a>. I suspect it has a lot to do with the fact that this story had more of the hands-on approach than the rest. Whereas the 'mystery' in the previous Corey book was solved in the last pages of the book, "Night Fall" was shrouded in mystery to the end and only slowly revealed its secrets.<br /><br />John Corey seemed to be more in his element in this book. Or perhaps, all that chasing around masked some of the cynicism and bravado. Don't get me wrong, I like his dry sense of humor and witty cynicism but it can be too much at times. Especially since he used it on everybody and everything, making me wonder at times if we really loved his wife or how much trust he had in some people. It took the last heart wrenching pages of the book to read about John and Kate's emotions without the veil of sarcasm.<br /><br />I loved the mystery of the book and John's deductive abilities as well as his 'fuck-you' attitude towards authority. It showed a world where good guys could win if they had good arguments, evidence and balls of steel. But it also portrayed America as victim, having the whole world against it (which I doubt).<br /><br />The ending of the book took me by surprise. I would have loved to see how the situation would have been resolved but since it was based on a true case, I suppose such twists and turns to the story wouldn't have been well received by the public. I was actually saddened by the list of friends lost but I guess it's just an sliver compared to the grief experienced after the Towers fell.<br /><br />Overall, it was a good book. Mystery, murder, conspiracy theories and a witty detective to solve the puzzle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15927426953227097846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2667618" />
    <a title="Erik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/168656-erik"><img alt="Erik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544542689p2/168656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2667618?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erik" href="/user/show/168656-erik">Erik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/1063356.Night_Fall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14991797182929120915">This was one of those novels that the pre-release hype was so great that as a reader, I was not sure what to expect but Night Fall with a few small exceptions lived up to the media hubbub. The novel starts with a flashback scene that takes us to the Atlantic coast on the fateful night of the TWA flight 800 crash. On the beach, two "consenting adults" are enjoying their night out and for posterity sake filmed the evening. On this tape, the "accident" and a strange shooting light is trapped on cel</span>
  <span id="freeText14991797182929120915" style="display:none">This was one of those novels that the pre-release hype was so great that as a reader, I was not sure what to expect but Night Fall with a few small exceptions lived up to the media hubbub. The novel starts with a flashback scene that takes us to the Atlantic coast on the fateful night of the TWA flight 800 crash. On the beach, two "consenting adults" are enjoying their night out and for posterity sake filmed the evening. On this tape, the "accident" and a strange shooting light is trapped on celluloid.<br /><br />Cut to five years later and we are introduced to FBI consultant John Corey and his wife Kate Mayfield, recurring characters from DeMille's other works. Mayfield having been an investigator at the original scene is concerned with eye witness discrepancies, the TSA's official cause and other miss steps. As her concern builds, her husband becomes interested as well.<br /><br />What follows is a tightly scripted story with twists at every turn right up until an explosive ending that can leave the reader with an adrenaline high or a sense of bewilderment. Overall, Night Fall was a wonderful read but may disappoint readers who are looking for answers and not just a compelling novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14991797182929120915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9696479412856468592">Provocative, frightening, and based on True Events.<br/> It is dusk on July 17, 1996. A man and a woman who are married - but not to each other - make love on a Long Island beach as a video camera records their pleasures...and something more. Out over the ocean, TWA flight 800 suddenly explodes with 230 victims on board, the terrible blast illuminating the sky. The government's verdict is mechanical failure. But the videotape may tell another story - if it can be found.<br/> Now, on the 5th anniversary of</span>
  <span id="freeText9696479412856468592" style="display:none">Provocative, frightening, and based on True Events.<br /> It is dusk on July 17, 1996. A man and a woman who are married - but not to each other - make love on a Long Island beach as a video camera records their pleasures...and something more. Out over the ocean, TWA flight 800 suddenly explodes with 230 victims on board, the terrible blast illuminating the sky. The government's verdict is mechanical failure. But the videotape may tell another story - if it can be found.<br /> Now, on the 5th anniversary of the crash, two memebers of the Federal Anti-Terrorist Task Force set out to reopen the case: John Corey, and ex-NYPD detective, and his wife, Kate Mayfield, a career FBI agent. Together, they hunt for the crucial video...and race toward an elusive truth even more horrifying thatn the crash itself.Love Nelson DeMille...a great story teller...and this John Corey guy has a fantastic dry sense of humor that keeps you chuckling. And checking the interenet to see if what they're talking about is REAL!!!!! YIKES! <br /><br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296613040" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296613040?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/6117137-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296613040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7430728297553918771">I had not read a DeMille book in a long time and while I liked this one (part of the John Corey series) I don't think it was as good as his earlier efforts, such as The General's Daughter and The Charm School (my personal favorites). The book had an e-x-t-r-e-m-e-l-y slow start and there were a few times when I thought I would just throw it aside and not finish. The clues to the mystery were too slow in coming and the author seemed to prefer to continually go over and over the aspects of the cra</span>
  <span id="freeText7430728297553918771" style="display:none">I had not read a DeMille book in a long time and while I liked this one (part of the John Corey series) I don't think it was as good as his earlier efforts, such as The General's Daughter and The Charm School (my personal favorites). The book had an e-x-t-r-e-m-e-l-y slow start and there were a few times when I thought I would just throw it aside and not finish. The clues to the mystery were too slow in coming and the author seemed to prefer to continually go over and over the aspects of the crash of TWA flight 800. I did not learn anything new each time he described the crash. In fact, I started skipping that part! Usually when a mystery author does that, they will plant a small clue or add another piece to the puzzle that's building. I just found it too repetitive. I did like the ending, it was a great tie it, but I won't give it away! No spoilers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7430728297553918771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12053101108765921851">This is my first Nelson DeMille book. It is not the typical genre I read, but this came highly recommended so I wanted to check it out. <br/><br/>The main character is written like your typical, arrogant, NY detective... so if you can get past the over the top machismo, this book is enjoyable. There were a couple of nice twists and turns and it definitely kept me interested. I would probably read more books by this author.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14186367013941006757">It's very uncommon for me to be reading thrillers. I like the genre, but there are other genres that are getting my attention a lot more. This book made me realise that I really should spend more time reading thriller/detectives.<br/><br/>What intrigued me the most about this book is the fact that it is a true story.   <span id="freeText14186367013941006757" style="display:none">It's very uncommon for me to be reading thrillers. I like the genre, but there are other genres that are getting my attention a lot more. This book made me realise that I really should spend more time reading thriller/detectives.<br /><br />What intrigued me the most about this book is the fact that it is a true story. In 1996 there was an airplane "shot down" after departing from NY and it did crash into the sea. To this day there is still a lot of questionmarks to what happened with this plane. <br /><br />From the beginning till the end this book grabbed my attention. The tension I felt was present on every page and I really like the character John Corey. I love his sarcasm. I read that some readers are a bit dissappointed by the ending, not me. I think it's very smart. How can a writer, who has based his book on a true story with so many conspiracy theories, "solve" the case in the end? <br /><br />Spoiler about the ending!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When the part came that Kate had to return from Tanzania on a plane I ggot the feeling that it had something to do with 9/11. I don't know why, because those planes didn't come from Tanzania. I can't remember if the author ever mentioned the month or date, but in the end I did see it coming that he would "silence" the case with the 9/11 disaster. Fitting end. The cause of the planecrash remains a mystery! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2136140383&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136140383" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10746177992358718231">Great ... until page 325 when the CIA "villain" came back to life and spoiled the show. The arc of the climax is similar to the ill-fated and sad flight of TWA Flight 800; a slow climb off the tarmac, not unlike a 747 lumbering down the runway. But when it gets to cruising speed shot down as it gained altitude. <br/><br/>The controversial CIA animation of "what really and truly happened" to TWA Flight 800 discounts entirely the actual eyewitness testimony of 250 people; all of whom can't be wrong here. I </span>
  <span id="freeText10746177992358718231" style="display:none">Great ... until page 325 when the CIA "villain" came back to life and spoiled the show. The arc of the climax is similar to the ill-fated and sad flight of TWA Flight 800; a slow climb off the tarmac, not unlike a 747 lumbering down the runway. But when it gets to cruising speed shot down as it gained altitude. <br /><br />The controversial CIA animation of "what really and truly happened" to TWA Flight 800 discounts entirely the actual eyewitness testimony of 250 people; all of whom can't be wrong here. I am not prone to conspiracy theories but something more than the "official" findings happened. Some day the whole truth will come out. God help us when it does.<br /><br />Well-written fictionalized account of an exceptionally sad event in our nation's history. Well worth the time. Sadly, we entered in to a dark alley on July 17, 1996 that we are still trying to come to terms with and work our way out of and away from. Something very wrong is going on in this country and on this planet. Only constant reading, education and vigilance by braver, smarter men and women than yours truly can set us free and back on the right path.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17295595342480727446"><i>Wow.</i><br/>I was not expecting that.<br/><br/>It was a rough start with this book. Although the characters were interesting and the mystery somewhat interesting as well (I'm just not very into espionage thrillers), it was reaaally slow and I quickly lost interest.<br/><br/>Because I hate DNF'ing books, I kept reading this one. And, <i>oh boy!</i>, did it pay off!<br/>I started falling in love even more with the characters. I'll give it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille' title='Nelson DeMille' rel='nofollow noopener'> Nelson DeMille</a>, he sure knows how to write and develop characters extremely well. <br/>And the myste</span>
  <span id="freeText17295595342480727446" style="display:none"><i>Wow.</i><br />I was not expecting that.<br /><br />It was a rough start with this book. Although the characters were interesting and the mystery somewhat interesting as well (I'm just not very into espionage thrillers), it was reaaally slow and I quickly lost interest.<br /><br />Because I hate DNF'ing books, I kept reading this one. And, <i>oh boy!</i>, did it pay off!<br />I started falling in love even more with the characters. I'll give it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" title="Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nelson DeMille</a>, he sure knows how to write and develop characters extremely well. <br />And the mystery? It just got more and more intriguing! The pace grew quicker and quicker and until it reached that AMAZING ending.<br /><br />I'll think more about this book in the next few days and, quite possibly, will pump the rating up to a 3.5, if not a 4 star rating. It's a really well done novel.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2613160354" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5522484710356282047">I wanted to give 3 stars to this book. But ending changed my minds. <br/>At first, it was a really slow reading. Main character was reviewing old evidence of a plane crash and it looked like it doesn't lead to anything. It got more interesting when the lost evidence were found and action became more hectic. <br/>But the ending was unexpected. <br/>There was not much of a book left already, but there were a lot of questions.   <span id="freeText5522484710356282047" style="display:none">I wanted to give 3 stars to this book. But ending changed my minds. <br />At first, it was a really slow reading. Main character was reviewing old evidence of a plane crash and it looked like it doesn't lead to anything. It got more interesting when the lost evidence were found and action became more hectic. <br />But the ending was unexpected. <br />There was not much of a book left already, but there were a lot of questions. Who hit the plane? What FBI is going to do? What will happen to the tape? What will happen to main characters? What will happen to witness? And most importantly, how THE MEETING will develop. I was confused how author will answer to all these questions in such a short number of pages which were left. <br />I paid attention that John decided to meet in a restaurant "Windows on the World", but I didn't know that it was 11th of September. I think that explains everything. <br />So while trying to figure out what happened to one plane, John witnessed another tragic event that really happened and changed the world as we knew it. I remember that day very vividly, no matter that I live an ocean away from New York. <br />The book is a quite typical crime story with <br /> a lack of fights and guns. But as I say, the ending is strong. The book is about global problems, not about random local murder. <br />In memory of those people who were killed "in the name of God".</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107144807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11388038875696831874">I really liked The Lion's Game so I quickly found which book came next and began reading it ... boy am I glad that I did. I enjoyed Night Fall even more than the prior book! And, since I gave it four stars -- and looking back I wouldn't change that rating -- I had to think about whether I could really rate a spy novel 5 stars. (I usually find that difficult to justify because there are many classics that I don't think deserve that rating.) But, I loved this book from beginning to end. I found th</span>
  <span id="freeText11388038875696831874" style="display:none">I really liked The Lion's Game so I quickly found which book came next and began reading it ... boy am I glad that I did. I enjoyed Night Fall even more than the prior book! And, since I gave it four stars -- and looking back I wouldn't change that rating -- I had to think about whether I could really rate a spy novel 5 stars. (I usually find that difficult to justify because there are many classics that I don't think deserve that rating.) But, I loved this book from beginning to end. I found the plot to be intricate and complex. I found John Corey to be funny, smart, and flawed. I enjoy his moments of breaking the fourth wall where he seems to speak directly to me. I enjoy his wit and sarcasm. I even like his pessimism and I am by nature an optimist. This is a truly good book.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18143583648877401578">16 books on my favorites list now 17 love DeMille and John Corey</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1224103760'><a id="like_count_review_1224103760" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1224103760?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F93788.Night_Fall">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3537194406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3537194406" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21965967-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449092263p2/21965967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3537194406?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/21965967-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40940631-night-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=male-authors">male-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21965967-amber?shelf=dude-lit">dude-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3537194406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14376114790221198313">I wondered repeatedly while vreading this, “What is the point of this story?” It's clearly not to tell the story of TWA Flight 800, which is a five-year-old closed case at the time our story opens. If you want the full story of the Flight 800 disaster, there are dozens, if not scores, of books that will tell that story in much greater detail. <br/><br/>I wondered for a while if it might be to explore one of the more popular conspiracy theories by playing with the fictional idea of a pair of mysterious wit</span>
  <span id="freeText14376114790221198313" style="display:none">I wondered repeatedly while vreading this, “What is the point of this story?” It's clearly not to tell the story of TWA Flight 800, which is a five-year-old closed case at the time our story opens. If you want the full story of the Flight 800 disaster, there are dozens, if not scores, of books that will tell that story in much greater detail. <br /><br />I wondered for a while if it might be to explore one of the more popular conspiracy theories by playing with the fictional idea of a pair of mysterious witnesses who may have filmed the disaster as it happened and may be in possession of the only video evidence of the mysterious streak of light reported by over two hundred witnesses, but discounted as a mass optical illusion in the official final report. Curiously, there's very little mystery or suspense involved in most of the story. You go in knowing all about these two witnesses and the tape they made, and most of the book is spent watching detective John Corey flounder around trying to find them and the tape five years after the fact. It's not until the final 20% or so that the pace picks up.<br /><br />On the other hand, so much of the story focuses on the day-to-day legwork of re-interviewing witnesses who already told their story years ago, and trying to find evidence that has been lost – or hidden – that I wondered if maybe it's primarily a story about what working a cold case is like, using the Flight 800 case as a framework, with a cover-up conspiracy angle tacked on to help make it a bestseller.<br /><br />It's hard not to notice the timing of the story. Published in 2004 – in other words, after 9/11. But it's set in July 2001, five years after the Flight 800 disaster, and just months before 9/11. So none of the characters know 9/11 is coming, but we the reader do know, and DeMille wants us to keep it in mind. There are lots of glib references to terrorist attacks like the USS Cole, the Tanzania embassy bombing, the 1993 World Trade Center bombing, and the idea that some guy named Osama bin Laden and a little-known terrorist group he runs called al-Qaeda is an increasing danger to U.S. security. There are even a couples of scenes involving the Windows on the World bar at the top of the World Trade Center, and an interlude where Corey and his wife, as punishment for their snooping, are dispatched to Aden (the site of the USS Cole bombing) and Dar es Salaam (the site of the Tanzania embassy bombing), where their investigations go absolutely nowhere. And as the story timeline eases into September 2001... <br /><br />Well, I'll just say a lot of readers say they hated the ending, but as a storytelling device, was it really any worse than the ending of, say, Raiders of the Lost Ark, where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[after being saved from the Nazis, the Ark of the Covenant is packed into a crate and shipped off into the bowels of an enormous government warehouse, never to be seen again <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? Or Contact, where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the video recording proving that Ellie Arroway really did travel in space travel and make contact with aliens is erased, allowing everyone to discredit and ignore her testimony <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? Or the original Ocean's 11, where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the criminal protagonists' plan to sneak the stolen money out in a coffin backfires, and they end up having to literally watch the money burn in a crematory oven <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? Or even, I dunno, Anna Karenina, where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the heroine's search for love and adventure ruins her life, and she ends up throwing herself in front of a train <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? The world isn't always a storybook ending where truth wins out, villains are brought to justice, and all the heroes go home happy, and I have a certain respect for an author who's brave enough not to pander to audiences who want everything to turn out rosy every time.<br /><br />All this made me wonder if maybe Night Fall is really a love letter to our pre-9/11 innocence and sense of invulnerability. Or maybe it's really an indictment of that same sense of invulnerability that led a complacent U.S. government to ignore the many clues in the months and years before 9/11 that anti-American terrorism was becoming an ever-more-present danger.<br /><br />Know going in the writing is ridiculously hard-boiled. John Corey is a tough, stubborn, whiskey-soaked, macho former NYPD detective with a scathing wisecrack for every occasion. There's actually a scene where the supe calls Corey in to bust his balls and literally calls him a “loose cannon.” I actually yelled, “OHHHHH, WHYYYY???” when I heard this. It's pretty bad. But it is fun.<br /><br /><b>Audio Notes:</b> This is one of a very small handful of audiobooks I've ever encountered that have a score/soundtrack. Mostly subtle music that sets the tone of a given scene, with a few low-key sound effects here and there that are mostly designed not to interfere with the narration. Scott Brick is a competent narrator and not one of my personal favorites, but I know a lot of people like him. I'll admit he's at his best here in a text that's a first-person POV narration by a crusty, sarcastic, middle-aged male ex-cop. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14376114790221198313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3206545982" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3206545982" />
    <a title="Jenifer Ruff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27083781-jenifer-ruff"><img alt="Jenifer Ruff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500589891p2/27083781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3206545982?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenifer Ruff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenifer Ruff" href="/user/show/27083781-jenifer-ruff">Jenifer Ruff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40940631-night-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3206545982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6506181206768628829">The writing is great and the main character is funny and clever. I enjoyed this book so much until the end when it went from a five star read to a four. I'd like to give it one star because I'm so unhappy with the ending, but that would imply the book was garbage and it certainly is not. The entire story is an investigation of what really happened to a jet that crashed in the ocean after taking off in NY. The main characters is out to discover the truth and why higher-ups in the FBI went to grea</span>
  <span id="freeText6506181206768628829" style="display:none">The writing is great and the main character is funny and clever. I enjoyed this book so much until the end when it went from a five star read to a four. I'd like to give it one star because I'm so unhappy with the ending, but that would imply the book was garbage and it certainly is not. The entire story is an investigation of what really happened to a jet that crashed in the ocean after taking off in NY. The main characters is out to discover the truth and why higher-ups in the FBI went to great lengths to derail the investigation and cover up the truth. But then we never find out the answer. Or at least I never did. Seriously, I was wondering and wondering and trying to guess. I couldn't wait to see what sort of explanation would explain away what we had learned. I would have been happy with something totally unbelievable as opposed to nothing. I would definitely read more by this author, and considering how famous he is, I'm sure he doesn't care either way, but the ending was a huge disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6506181206768628829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9mw/3Pkt/GeMlaZGA9vYtfn4KMGT/yormOjD54+GOssD0CNjoO6GkS0D0kSEfvpBzYgaFWoPawMctrdS/6lMBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e+1lfKZE/K9SBOE4NBmCQinupKbPwr0mCklZA2UTYtGOUXnD/4eGWfOSlTqzvKC2HZ6WcjYy/A6OFy22FTwUHA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">About Nelson DeMille</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1498066748p3/1238.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">Nelson DeMille
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,330
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1569496128689428859">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br/><br/>DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United S</span>
  <span id="freeText1569496128689428859" style="display:none">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69). He saw action in Vietnam as an infantry platoon leader with the First Cavalry Division and was decorated with the Air Medal, Bronze Star, and the Vietnamese Cross of Gallantry.<br /><br />After his discharge, DeMille returned to Hofstra University where he received his bachelor’s degree in Political Science and History. He has three children, Lauren, Alexander, and James, and resides on Long Island.<br /><br />DeMille's first major novel was By the Rivers of Babylon, published in 1978, and is still in print as are all his succeeding novels. He is a member of American Mensa, The Authors Guild, and is past president of the Mystery Writers of America. He is also a member of International Thriller Writers and was chosen as ThrillerMaster of the Year 2015. He holds three honorary doctorates: Doctor of Humane Letters from Hofstra University, Doctor of Literature from Long Island University, and Doctor of Humane Letters from Dowling College.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is the author of: By the Rivers of Babylon, Cathedral, The Talbot Odyssey, Word of Honor, The Charm School, The Gold Coast, The General's Daughter, Spencerville, Plum Island, The Lion's Game, Up Country, Night Fall, Wild Fire, The Gate House, The Lion, The Panther, The Quest, Radiant Angel, The Cuban Affair and The Deserter. He also co-authored Mayday with Thomas Block and has contributed short stories to anthologies, and book reviews and articles to magazines and newspapers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1569496128689428859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
